Current Affairs Commentary

Unity and Responsibility (2)

-- Yuan

Yesterday, the meaning of unity and responsibility was discussed, and it was said that the central government has already assumed responsibility for facing the difficult situation. Today, the most difficult situation that the government must face is to work hard on suppressing bandits. However, bandit suppression cannot rely solely on the troops at the front. On the one hand, efforts should be made to prevent unexpected incidents at home from hindering the work of bandit suppression. On the other hand, local authorities in all provinces and regions should work hard to prevent bandits from infiltrating and to eliminate bandits in the rear to ensure the safety of the local people. And the local people should also work together to support all the work in the rear, and maintaining the security of the rear is an indirect way of assisting in bandit suppression. If this can be done, the task of bandit suppression will surely succeed easily. However, this cannot be done without national unity first.

The so-called unexpected incidents at home refer to the brewing of the Fujian Incident that has been rumored recently. However, the news of this Fujian Incident and the inside story are still unclear. If the brewing is indeed as publicized, and if this brewing does not work after open and honest mediation, then the government must suppress it with force. The use of force will inevitably lead to conflict, and conflict will inevitably devastate the region and cause suffering to the people. Not only will the people suffer, but the work of bandit suppression will also be affected, causing delays in the work that is about to be completed. Therefore, in today's tight situation, internal strife must not be allowed to occur again. Moreover, it is said that the center of the brewing of the Fujian Incident is the 19th Route Army. The 19th Route Army's resistance to Japan has won the sympathy of the whole nation, and people are rushing to help them because they can save the country. After the war, they also stated that they would not participate in civil war, which showed that they had no other intentions other than resisting Japan, and was especially appreciated by the people. Now, the news of the Fujian Incident has suddenly spread, which is truly shocking. Because today, the reason why the government is paying special attention to bandit suppression is precisely to save the country. If internal strife breaks out again, hindering the work of bandit suppression, it will not only be inconsistent with the purpose of not participating in civil war, but also seem to contradict the meaning of saving the country. If it is said that the government's approach cannot save the country, then try asking the 19th Route Army what approach it will take to save the country. To plan a coup without an approach is no different from those who are focused on creating chaos. The people have suffered from the ravages of war for a long time, and they have suffered deeply from the disasters of floods, droughts, and bandits. At present, they only seek to survive and do not want any further actions in the region that would hinder their security. Therefore, in the past, when the people heard about the 19th Route Army's resistance to Japan, they could not help but rejoice and rush to provide assistance, but now, because of participating in civil war, they will reverse their previous attitude. How could the 19th Route Army have no one who understands the stakes and act so recklessly? This is something that we cannot understand deeply. Therefore, before the true nature of the content is fully clarified, we dare not rashly make excessive speculation and definitive judgments, and it is enough to wait for a clear announcement in the future before commenting further.

We will now set aside the Fujian Incident and focus on the responsibility of local authorities in all provinces for bandit suppression, which is also very important. Today's bandit suppression work not only relies on the progress of the central front-line troops, but also depends on the concerted efforts of provinces such as Guangdong and Fujian. If the concerted attack is not strong enough, not only will the front-line troops not receive assistance, but they may also be disrupted, hindering the progress of the front. This is what the troops in all provinces and regions should strive for. As for the general population, they all hope to overcome national difficulties, carry out all kinds of construction, develop industry and commerce, and ensure local order and stability. However, the first step must be the success of bandit suppression. To achieve success in bandit suppression, the people in the rear must rise up together to make efforts to provide assistance. To have the people provide assistance together, the current situation of disunity cannot be of any help. Therefore, we must first encourage the spirit of unity and rise up to jointly shoulder this important responsibility.

German and Soviet Delegations Abandon Original Claims: Self-Government Organization May Be Abandoned; Tianchi to Establish Self-Government Discussion Conference; Ikizaka Hiroshi and Others Inspect the Urad League

Tomorrow, various princes will come to Suiyuan with Huang and Zhao to participate in a joint celebration.

Guihua: Prince Te and Prince Yun have abandoned their claim to organize a self-governing government and are willing to proceed according to the plan set by the central government. Currently, various princes are about to establish an Inner Mongolia self-government discussion conference in Tianchi to prepare for everything. The princes in Bailingmiao are scheduled to come to Suiyuan with Huang on the 20th to participate in the Mongolian-Han joint celebration. Ikizaka Hiroshi and others departed on the 18th to inspect the Urad League. (18th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qin Decun will go to Suiyuan to meet Huang and discuss the Inner Mongolia self-government issue. Qin will go after Huang returns to Suiyuan from the temple. (18th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Zhangjia previously sent Li Shoushan and Gong Ziwan to Mongolia for investigation. Li and Gong telegraphed from Ping that the investigation has been completed and they are expected to arrive in Ping around the 20th of this month. After Zhang returns to Ping with Li and Gong, he will be able to decide on the departure date. (18th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Bai Yunti said that he received a telegram from Huang yesterday, saying that the consultations with Prince Te, Prince Yun, and others in Bailingmiao were satisfactory. Recently, because Prince Te has accepted the central government's plan and abandoned the original proposal for an Inner Mongolia self-governing government, he has proposed a new plan for discussion. He will leave the temple around the 20th of this month and return to Suiyuan. The content of the new proposal is roughly divided into two items: (1) The issue of Inner Mongolia self-government. The representatives of various leagues and banners of Inner Mongolia previously resolved at a meeting in Bailingmiao to adopt a self-governing government system, directly under the central government and the Suiyuan and Chahar provincial governments, as parallel agencies. The Suiyuan provincial authorities advocate that it be under the jurisdiction of the provincial government. (2) The scope of the self-governing region. The northern part of Chahar, the Xilingol League, the Urad League north of the Daqing Mountains, the Ordos League in the Hetao area, and the Tumeds in the west will be designated as self-governing regions. Huang and Zhao will return to Suiyuan after the above issues have been discussed and resolved. The Suiyuan and Chahar authorities will exchange opinions and return to Beijing to decide on the entire plan. After Huang returns to Suiyuan, he plans to hold a Han-Mongolian joint celebration, but it is difficult to predict whether the various princes of Inner Mongolia will come to Suiyuan to participate. Zhangjia has telegraphed back to Prince Te and others, stating that he will stay in Ping due to business and will not go to Mongolia for the time being. He expressed his support for Inner Mongolia's self-government. He will go to Mongolia after meeting with Minister Huang in Ping. (18th Dispatch)

Procedures for Receiving Shanhaiguan: Ping Authorities Send Tao and Zhu as Representatives to Negotiate with the Japanese Army in Tianjin and Shanhaiguan

(Beiping) After the principles for receiving the passes of the Great Wall are determined, it is urgent to proceed. After recent consultations between the two sides, it will start with the reception of Shanhaiguan. The authorities have now appointed Tao Shangming and Zhu Shiqin as representatives to go to Shanhaiguan to negotiate the reception procedures with the Japanese army stationed in Shanhaiguan. Tao and Zhu are scheduled to go to Tianjin tomorrow morning to have consultations with the Hebei Provincial Government. They will leave for Shanhaiguan from Tianjin with representatives of the provincial government and Japanese liaison personnel on the same day. When passing through Haiyangzhen, Zhang Shousong, the magistrate of Linyu County, and the chief of the Linyu Public Security Bureau will also accompany them. After arriving in Shanhaiguan, they will formally negotiate the reception procedures of Shanhaiguan with the Japanese military representative Staff Officer Endo. The reception will begin as soon as the reception procedures have been negotiated. (18th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Chai Mountain urged the Political Committee to take over because the Japanese army in Shanhaiguan had been withdrawing to Jinzhou one after another. Huang Fu sent Tao Shangming to handle it. Tao is scheduled to go to Tianjin tomorrow to first contact Nakamura, the commander of the North China Garrison Army, because the garrison in Shanhaiguan is under the jurisdiction of the Tianjin Garrison Army. Tao will transfer from Tianjin to Shanhaiguan to discuss with Endo after contacting Nakamura. After the consultation, the Linyu County Office can move into the old office in the city to work. The security in the city is the responsibility of the Changli Security Team. Currently, the 14th Mixed Brigade troops in Shanhaiguan, Beidaihe, and Qinhuangdao have been transferred to the northern part of Manchuria. Only a garrison of more than 200 people remains in Shanhaiguan. (18th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Yin Rugeng said that the security teams at the major passes of the Great Wall have mostly arrived one after another. The local administration is under my exercise of power and is in fact the reception. There are many small passes on the Great Wall, and the security teams cannot fully reach each pass for garrison for a while. The Japanese army has not withdrawn because it cannot find houses temporarily. The Japanese Kwantung Army promised to return Shanhaiguan first, and we have sent personnel to negotiate within days. The Jizhou-Miyun Commissioner's Office is preparing to set up an office in Miyun to facilitate contact with the Japanese at any time. (18th Dispatch)

Yu Xuezhong Flies to Ping: The Bandit Troubles in Eastern Luan Are Expected to Be Completely Eliminated Soon

(Beiping) Yu Xuezhong arrived in Ping this afternoon. He will meet Huang and He in days to report on important matters. Large groups of bandits in eastern Luan have left the Great Wall and fled to the Lingnan area in Rehe. Other small groups can also be wiped out. The bandit troubles in eastern Luan are expected to be completely eliminated soon. It was previously reported that Shanhaiguan may be received this month, but the latest situation is unknown. The military pay for the North China Army reported by Hebei Province was originally 500,000 yuan per month, but in recent years, many tax revenues in the war zone have been exempted, and the three counties in southern Hebei have suffered floods. In addition, the incorporation of the troops of Li Jichun, Shi Yousan, and others, and the pay for the security teams have been borne by the provincial government at 470,000 yuan. In the future, the expenses for the security teams and others in eastern Luan will still require 200,000 yuan per month. Therefore, only 200,000 yuan can be reported each month. If the order in the counties recovers and income improves after six months, more may be transferred. Lu Muting went to Beijing earlier to report to the central government on the financial difficulties and expenditures of Hebei Province. He has now returned to Tianjin. Song is gradually recovering from his waist disease in Tianjin. It is heard that he will stay in Tianjin for some time. (18th Dispatch)

Results of the Regular Higher Examination Announced

(Nanjing) The scores of the regular examination papers of the Second Higher Examination have all been calculated. There are 31 people in general administration, 11 in financial administration, 10 in educational administration, 9 in accounting administration, 4 in statistics, 5 in diplomats and consuls, and 32 in judicial officials. There are a total of 2 women, all of whom are judicial officials. It is heard that most of the top names in each category are from verification trial personnel and few are from schools. The results were announced at 3:00 PM on the 18th, and interviews will be held in Nanjing on the same day. (18th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The results of the regular examination of the Second Higher Examination were announced at 3:00 PM on the afternoon of the 18th. 102 people, including Xu Jiaqi, were admitted. There were 2 women, 121 imperial administrative personnel, 11 financial personnel, 10 education personnel, 9 accounting personnel, 4 statistical personnel, 5 diplomats and consuls, and 32 judicial officials. The place of origin was Jiangsu 27, Zhejiang 20, Hunan 10, Fujian 8, Shandong 3, Hebei 12, Hubei 3, Yunnan 1, Jiangxi 1, Jilin 1, Guangdong 1, Anhui 7, Sichuan 3, Henan 1, Guizhou 1, Chahar 1, and Shanxi 1. The age was mostly between 24 and 30 years old, and there were only 2 people over 42 years old. The oral examination is scheduled to be held on the 24th. The members admitted in Beiping will arrive in Beijing within days to participate. (18th Central News Agency Dispatch)

The Boundary Dispute Between Nanjing City and Jiangning County Has Not Been Resolved

(Nanjing) The boundary demarcation issue between the Nanjing Municipal Government and Jiangning County has been in dispute for a long time and has not yet been resolved. Jiangning County's reason is that it is currently a self-governing experimental county focusing on construction. It firmly claims that the original demarcation of the city area hinders county governance and must be changed. As for the registration and transfer of books, etc., these are all matters for later. The reason of the Municipal Government is that various taxes and levies in the city have been successively opened, but only the land tax has not been collected because the household name atlas has not been approved for transfer by the Jiangning County Government. Before the demarcation by the provincial government is completed, the management power of the city only extends to the scope of the Capital Police Department. Within this scope, those households who should have paid the land tax earlier have not paid to the city. Jiangning County is afraid that it will be difficult to collect taxes beyond its authority. If this is delayed for a long time, this land tax will be invisibly lost once the land is transferred. The issue was raised for discussion at the municipal meeting on the 18th, and it was resolved to urge Jiangning County to quickly hand over the collection books for collection. It was also said that the Jiangsu Provincial Government had agreed to the transfer of the books, but Jiangning County was unwilling to do so immediately. The Municipal Government will take effective measures to urge the county to comply. (18th Dispatch)

Jingxing Coal Mine Workers' Strike: Workers Decide to Go on Strike Due to Unsuccessful Demands; All Sectors Convene a Meeting to Discuss Mediation Methods

(Tianjin) The workers of the Jingxing Zhenfeng Coal Mine had previously negotiated with the factory regarding their demands for a salary increase and payment of back wages, but there has been no reply so far. The county party headquarters specially convened a meeting of all sectors on the 17th to discuss mediation methods. (18th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Liu Eqing and Others Draft Opinions on Rectifying the Opium Prohibition

There are even methods of supervising the sale of opium, which is equivalent to open sales, which ultimately leads to the judicial and administrative aspects often conflicting in their views on opium prohibition incidents. Liu and others are drafting an opinion letter, scheduling a discussion meeting of all supervisory committee members next Thursday to exchange opinions, and appointing personnel to be responsible for drafting. After Yu Youren returns to Beijing to review it, they will make suggestions to the central government or accommodate the facts, simply change the opium prohibition law, and stipulate the order of phased prohibition, so as to avoid the current opium prohibition law being equivalent to a mere formality. (18th Dispatch)

US-Russia Negotiations Successful: Roosevelt Goes to Hot Springs

(Washington) President Roosevelt has already set off to rest at the hot springs. The exchange of notes between Roosevelt and Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov has just been published. Litvinov gave a written guarantee that Soviet policy would thoroughly respect the right of the United States to determine its own existence. The Soviet Union absolutely does not interfere in the affairs of the United States and its territories. The Soviet government will stop all propaganda made by Soviet officials or personnel directly or indirectly managed by the Soviet government, the purpose of which is to infringe on American territory or change the American political organization by violence. In addition to the Washington government, all groups claiming to represent the American government or seeking to overthrow the American government by violence are not allowed to exist in the Soviet Union or to engage in the organization of various organizations within the Soviet Union. Those who aim to use violence to overthrow the American political and social order are also not allowed to exist in the Soviet Union. In President Roosevelt's reply, he guaranteed that the United States would follow the same policy towards the Soviet Union. In addition, there is another note that specifically discusses religious issues. The Soviet Union allows American citizens to build churches in the Soviet Union, and the houses used can receive donations for religious purposes. The two sides also exchanged views on the establishment of consular treaties, the application of most-favored-nation treatment, and the protection of overseas Chinese. Even the Soviet government has the right to file a lawsuit for the private debts that the previous governments of Russia could demand from the United States, and it is now acknowledged to be abandoned. (Havas Dispatch, 17th)

(Washington) In the exchange of notes between Roosevelt and Litvinov, although the Soviet government gave up its demands on the US intervention in Siberia, this intervention does not include the US intervention in Archangelsk. The Soviet government still maintains its demands on the US regarding this intervention. According to reports, in 1918, the US government sent 7,000 troops to land in Vladivostok, with the aim of preventing German prisoners in the area from rearming to resist the Allied forces, so it sent an expeditionary force. At that time, the commander of the American expeditionary force was ordered to maintain strict neutrality in the conflict between the White Russians and the Red Russians, but after 4,700 American troops landed in Archangelsk, they actually participated in the battle against the Soviet army. During this expedition, 200 American soldiers were killed and 300 were injured. (Havas Dispatch, 18th)

Russian Embassy Red Flag Waving in the Wind

(Washington) The most prominent sign of the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia is that the red flag of the Soviet Union was hoisted above the Russian Embassy here this afternoon. The embassy was officially handed over to Litvinov by the State Department today. (National Telegram, 15th)

Japan Pretends to Be Calm

(Tokyo) According to the Tokyo Daily News this morning, the United States recognized Russia yesterday, and Litvinov and Roosevelt issued a joint statement. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs said that the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia has a great impact on the European political situation. It is not surprising that the United States and Russia are trying to get closer for the sake of their own economic recovery. There are rumors that the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia is intended to contain Japan's policy toward China and change the peaceful policy in the Far East, but Japan's policy toward Russia still takes peaceful means to resolve disputes between the two countries, so the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia has nothing to do with Japan. This is how the Japanese side is trying to maintain a calm attitude. (United China News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Worried About US-Russia Military Cooperation

(Tokyo) Regarding the issue of the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a statement today saying that although the main reason for the United States' recognition of Russia is to seek commercial interests, it may also be intended to contain Japan's actions in the Far East, but it will not drastically change its attitude toward Japan. There are rumors that after the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia, Russia will withdraw its proposal to sell the China Eastern Railway, which will not become a reality. Military cooperation may be brought up again, but even if it is a rumor, it must be taken into account. The United States, Russia, and China will be closer in 1936 than they are now. (United China News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

(Tokyo) According to the Tokyo Daily News, the United States and Russia discussed the issue of Japanese aggression against Russian territory during the negotiations for the restoration of diplomatic relations. The Japanese believe that the US President agreed to guarantee that Russia would maintain its national borders in the Far East, intending to jointly defend against Japan. The seventh document exchanged between the two countries and Litvinov's speech prove the truth of this matter. (United China News Agency Dispatch, 17th)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is watching the impact of the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia on the Far Eastern political situation, and its general observations are as follows: (1) There is no doubt that the United States intends to use the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia as a means of containing Japan, but President Roosevelt will not, therefore, make the policy toward Japan a concrete reinforcement. (2) On the contrary, the Soviet Union, by inducing the United States to assist the Soviet Union, especially to strengthen its attitude toward Japan, will gain a great deal. For example, the recent rumors of the withdrawal of the North Manchuria Railway negotiations, although they may be a propaganda effect, are also an expression of this. (3) It is still unclear whether the United States and Russia can establish an agreement against Japan in the future, but there are rumors that a secret agreement was signed last July, when the United States recognized the Soviet Union in exchange for the establishment of military interests in Kamchatka. Also, the United States, in view of its deep fear of Japan occupying the coastal province of Soviet Russia, Japan must pay attention to this. (4) As a result of the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia, China's attitude toward Japan will not change abruptly. (5) Japan, according to the decision of the Five Ministers' Conference, gives first priority to the development of Manchuria, but as a precautionary measure, it should implement diplomatic work with the United States, China, and Russia. (Electric News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

Military Authorities Say Japan Is Not Under Any Threat

(Tokyo) The Japanese Army authorities' observations on the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia are as follows: They express their deep congratulations for the sake of world peace. Since they do not know the conditions for the restoration of diplomatic relations, they cannot elaborate. The debts of the past may be gradually resolved. As for the impact of the rapprochement between the United States and Russia on Japan, it is expected that it will not be worse than it is today. (Electric News Agency Dispatch, 16th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Navy Ministry authorities issued a statement today saying that the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia was a matter of time and is not surprising, but Japan will not be threatened in any way by the US-Russia tie-up, and the United States and Russia will not change their attitude toward Japan for the sake of restoring diplomatic relations. (United China News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

Russia's Attitude Toward Japan Will Become Increasingly Strong

(Tokyo) The United States and Russia cleared up the 16-year state of severance and formally restored diplomatic relations, and all parties in Japan are paying the greatest attention to the future. The handshake and cooperation between the Soviet Union, the only proletarian dictatorship in the world today, and the capitalist country of the United States is a very interesting issue in international politics. A certain aspect of Japan anticipates the future as follows: The conditions for the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia were not specific items such as the conclusion of a non-aggression treaty or the establishment of a huge credit system, so in reality, there will be no immediate special impact. However, the scope of negotiations between the Soviet Union and other countries, such as debt issues, and the negation of religion, an important principle of communism, the Soviet Union must use this restoration of diplomatic relations to implement plans, and its direct and indirect impact is by no means small. The Soviet Union will definitely strengthen its attitude toward Europe in the future, and especially its attitude toward the Far East will be even stronger. The negotiations for the sale of the China Eastern Railway will inevitably be delayed as a result, and as a result of its strong attitude toward Manchukuo, various problems may occur between the two sides one after another. However, the United States has abandoned the so-called Stimson Doctrine on the Far East issue, and its decided policy is not to actively interfere in various issues unless American interests are infringed upon. It is also transferring the Pacific Fleet to the Atlantic Ocean in order to ease the atmosphere between the United States and Japan, so what kind of active attitude can it take in the Far East? The most significant impact on the Far East and the world as a result of the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia is that the Soviet Union will use the United States' abundant financial resources to carry out economic construction and industrial plans in order to redize China, India, and other countries. (Japan United News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

Japan's Policy Toward the Puppet State Remains Unchanged

(Changchun) Regarding the US recognition of Soviet Russia, the Manchukuo military and political authorities said the following: Even if the United States recognizes Soviet Russia, the military and political authorities do not consider it a problem. It is the trend of the times that capitalist America recognizes communist Soviet Russia. Manchukuo must further cooperate with Japan based on its established policy to deal with the situation. Only in the worst-case scenario is there better effort in strengthening national defense. (Electric News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

(Changchun) Regarding the US-Russia restoration of diplomatic relations, Hoshino, Chief of the General Affairs Division of the Ministry of Finance, said that the United States' recognition of Soviet Russia is a natural thing and has no economic impact on Manchukuo. The economic relations between Russia and Manchukuo are gradually improving, and relations with the United States are also turning better. Therefore, Manchukuo will always maintain its relations with Europe and the United States in accordance with the fundamental policy of open doors and equal opportunities. (Electric News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

A Coolant for the Tense Situation in the Far East: League of Nations Members Express Welcome

(Geneva) Geneva tonight welcomes the restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia. League of Nations members believe that this move can automatically reduce the possibility of conflict in the Far East, but regret that both countries have not joined the League of Nations. Foreign policy considerations are the important reasons for the rapprochement between the two countries. The Soviet Union is deeply afraid that Japan will take control of the situation in the Far East, or even engage in combat. President Roosevelt's warm reception of Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov is nothing short of a warning to Japan. In general, it is believed that the rapprochement between the United States and Russia will be beneficial to world peace. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Japan's Budget Difficulties: Army and Navy Demand Full Amount Be Approved

(Tokyo) The Ministry of the Army submitted its requests for reinstatement to the Ministry of Finance before the 20th. The contents are roughly as follows: (1) The assessed amount for the Manchurian Incident expenses is 123 million, but a reinstatement of the requested amount of 156 million is demanded. (2) The assessed amount for material maintenance expenses is 80 million, but the requested amount of 150 million is demanded. (3) A reinstatement of the entirely eliminated fuel research fee of 5 million from other new requests is demanded. The total amount of the reinstatement request is approximately 108 million. (Dentsu dispatch, 18th)

(Tokyo) Each cabinet member deeply understands Finance Minister Takahashi's difficulties regarding the Ministry of Finance's major cuts to the next year's budget. However, there is considerable dissatisfaction within the Navy Department and the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry. Negotiations for reinstatement requests will be conducted with the financial authorities within a day or two. If Finance Minister Takahashi completely disregards the intentions of the Five Ministers' Conference and the Internal Affairs Conference, there is a risk of triggering a political crisis. Therefore, Prime Minister Saito is also deeply concerned and will not go for his usual weekend rest on the 18th but will quietly observe the situation. He may personally step in to mediate between Finance Minister Takahashi, Navy Minister Osumi, and Agriculture Minister Goto. Thus, the budget cabinet meeting on the 21st has been postponed to the 24th. (Dentsu dispatch, 18th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Navy held a department meeting today to deliberate on budget countermeasures. An extraordinary meeting will be held tomorrow, even though it is a Sunday. Of the ¥690 million budget requested by the Navy Department, ¥262 million was cut by the Ministry of Finance. Only ¥178 million was approved for military expansion expenses, which is far from the original plan. Furthermore, the Ministry of Finance changed the two-year plan for the aviation corps, scheduled to be completed in 1936, to a five-year plan to be completed in 1939. The Navy authorities believe that this violates the resolutions of the Five Ministers' Conference and shows a lack of understanding of the international crisis. Only the refurbishment of battleships was approved for warship refurbishment expenses, and the refurbishment of aircraft carriers and cruisers was not approved. Among the 53 vessels outside treaty limitations, the Ministry of Finance only approved 15. It is questioned how such a situation can cope with the Pacific crisis in 1936. A decision was made to demand approval of the full amount, and the Vice Minister and Director of the Bureau of Accounting will contact the Ministry of Finance. Navy Minister Osumi will also personally visit Finance Minister Takahashi to seek a political solution. (United China News Agency dispatch, 18th)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received its budget for the next fiscal year from the Ministry of Finance on the 17th. The contents include the cancellation of important expenses such as the establishment of new departments and the establishment of additional embassies abroad. Of the ¥26.7 million in new expenses requested, only ¥8.9 million was approved. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' budget for the next fiscal year is recorded below (unit: ¥1,000):

Total Budget: 26,700, of which Regular Department: 17,600, Temporary Department: 9,100. Total amount of new budget requests: 8,900, of which Regular Department: 1,800, Temporary Department: 7,100. Important expenses in the new budget requests are as follows: (1) Exchange Rate Related Expenses: 26,800; (2) International Contributions and Others: 1,280; (3) Construction Expenses: 100; (4) Immigration Protection Fees: 400; (5) Increased Subsidy for Overseas Schools: 90; (6) Manchurian Incident Expenses: 3,700; (7) New Establishment of the Afghan Embassy: 100; (8) New Establishment of the South American Berri Consulate Branch: 30; (9) New Establishment of the Chengde Consulate: 40; (10) New Establishment of the Tumen Consulate Branch: 30. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has now decided to request the Ministry of Finance to reinstate the following expenses: Expenses for establishing the American Affairs Bureau: 110; Expenses for establishing the International Culture Bureau: 1,920; Temporary Investigation Department for Disarmament Treaty: 100; Expenses for establishing the Colombian Consulate: 120; Expenses for establishing Consulates-General and Consulates Branches: 500; Overseas Commerce Promotion Fees: 800; Diplomatic Work Awards: 3,000; Other Expenses: 6,000. Totaling 12,550 (Japan Union News Agency dispatch, 18th)

(National Telegraph, 17th)

(Washington) The US government has decided to temporarily abandon the plan to purchase 3 billion gold dollars worth of government bonds in the open market through the Federal Reserve Bank before the gold dollar movement produces results. Officials in the Ministry of Finance claim that suspending the purchase of government bonds is unimportant because only 800 million gold dollars have been purchased so far. If the government's plan to issue new bonds to replace old bonds encounters difficulties, it can still resume purchasing. However, some observers of current events claim that this move is due to the Federal Reserve Bank's refusal to support the government bond market after a split in opinions within the government on the monetary plan. Others hold the opposite view, believing that the Gold Purchase Plan of the Finance Rehabilitation Company is intended to supplement the open market securities purchase plan. Today, they held a monetary conference here, supporting the US President's plan to raise the price of gold and lower the price of the gold dollar. However, they advised the government to expand its policy and include silver as a national currency reserve. According to Senator Pittman, President Roosevelt is now willing to consider the proposal to mint silver coins using domestically produced silver. However, because there are many currency proposals from all parties, and their contents often vary greatly, the President is currently considering several silver coin minting proposals. We should give them a chance to experiment and not pressure them too much. (National Telegraph, 17th)

French Fiscal Policy: Budget Strives for Balance

(Paris) Finance Minister Bonnet said today at a meeting of the Finance Committee of the House of Representatives that it is extremely important to balance the budget, saying that it is urgently necessary to maintain public trust, especially because the United States is conducting monetary experiments. He estimates that the Ministry of Finance will need to raise an additional 17 billion francs in 1934, and may have to rely on borrowing to raise them. Bonnet also said that the United States has actually stopped buying gold, and the stability of the franc has not been affected. If the budget案 can be balanced and the position of the Treasury can be secured, then financial difficulties will naturally not occur. The committee meeting is still held as usual, non-publicly. Hungary and the League of Nations: Whether to Withdraw Has Not Yet Been Determined

(Berlin) Former Hungarian Prime Minister Count Bethlen gave a speech to the local stock exchange, saying that since various countries are unwilling to actually recognize Germany's equal rights to armaments, and are delaying its implementation through various methods, Germany's withdrawal from the League of Nations does not need to seek anyone's understanding. He also said that whether Hungary will withdraw from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference has not yet been definitively decided, but it wants to avoid hasty actions. As for rumors about the danger of war, "There is danger only if France and the Little Entente countries are determined to provoke armed conflict." Bethlen also advocated using peaceful means to amend various peace treaties. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

British and French Foreign Ministers Arrive in Geneva: Italian Representative and Czech Foreign Minister Have Also Departed. Parisian Public Opinion Strongly Advocates Direct Negotiations with Germany: France Submits Strict Military Supervision Plan to Disarmament Conference: Four-Power Conference Will Be Abandoned Due to French Opposition

(Geneva) The chances of negotiating disarmament with Germany outside of Geneva have greatly decreased today. French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour told reporters that France believes that the drafting of a disarmament convention should continue in Geneva. Therefore, informed observers generally believe that it is clearly difficult to reach an agreement with Germany under the current circumstances. Simon and Eden both met with Henderson this afternoon, and Paul-Boncour visited Simon and Henderson separately in the afternoon. (National Telegraph, 18th)

(Geneva) Three major European politicians arrived here in succession today to assist Henderson in rescuing the collapsing Disarmament Conference. The three were British Foreign Secretary Simon, British Undersecretary Eden, both from London, and French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour, who was invited by Simon and Eden when they passed through Paris. It is heard that Simon visited Henderson in the morning, urging him not to lose heart. (National Telegraph, 18th)

(Geneva) British Foreign Secretary Simon and Undersecretary Eden both arrived at the office of the Chairman of the Disarmament Conference at noon today. Henderson, Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, immediately received them. The two sides talked for a long time. People here claim that this meeting was only a courtesy visit, but under the current circumstances, since various accidents occurred in Britain this week, affecting its internal affairs, this kind of talk can be regarded as having substance. British representatives have not yet agreed with French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour on a meeting time, and are expected to meet in the afternoon. In addition, de Laguna, Chief of Staff of the Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, has reportedly departed for Geneva to replace the country's representative, Aloisi. Foreign offices of various countries are working hard to urge this gentleman to come so that he can contact representatives from various countries. A spokesman for the British delegation declared that there was no truth to the trips of Foreign Secretary Simon and Undersecretary Eden to Rome. Moreover, the idea of moving the Presidium of the Disarmament Conference to another location is inappropriate and impossible to realize. Czech Foreign Minister Piniés, the General Rapporteur of the Disarmament Conference, has now left the Czech capital and is expected to arrive here early on Sunday. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

(Geneva) French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour issued a statement upon arriving in Geneva, saying that we have absolutely not changed anything. Although Germany unfortunately withdrew from the Disarmament Conference, it will not affect our established policies. British Foreign Secretary Simon and Undersecretary Eden have already arrived here, and Czech Foreign Minister Piniés will arrive soon. The Italian representative, de Saragna, Chief of Staff of Prime Minister Mussolini, will also come here. The Disarmament Conference will resume active work based on the foundations we obtained last month, without any hindrance, and this is a genuine opportunity to produce a suitable disarmament convention. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Rome According to today's official statement, the Italian Chief Representative to the League of Nations, Aloisi, was unable to go to Geneva to meet British Foreign Secretary Simon and French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour due to being busy. The Italian government has decided to send Saragna instead. (Reuters dispatch, 17th)

Czech Capital Foreign Minister Piniés, the General Rapporteur of the Disarmament Conference, is scheduled to depart for Geneva the day after tomorrow and will stay for several days. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

(Geneva) The Special Committee for Discussing the Supervision of Armaments has now proposed a new French supervision plan, the purpose of which is to conduct strict checks to ensure the proper implementation of the Disarmament Convention. The plan lists three types of supervision: (1) Supervision of documents, which specifically reports the number of troops and combat products, and issues licenses for the manufacture of munitions; (2) Supervision of expenses; (3) Supervision of on-site inspections, and proposes not only periodic, automatic, and permanent supervision, but also sudden investigations without prior notice to avoid eliminating unfavorable evidence. (Reuters dispatch, 17th)

Naval Competition Between Britain, the United States, and Japan: Japan Increases Navy Personnel by 40,000: The United States Increases by 39,700

(London) The British Naval Minister answered questions in the House of Commons today comparing the number of naval personnel in various countries around the world. It is said that since 1914, the United States has increased by 39,700 people, and Japan has increased by about 30,000 people, while Britain alone has decreased by about 55,400 people. (National Telegraph, 17th)

Two Famous British Figures Oppose Further Reducing Armaments: Restore 1933 Shipbuilding Program

(London) Last night, many famous British figures discussed the issue of disarmament. Churchill spoke at a political meeting, still strongly opposing further disarmament talks, saying that it is harmful and useless. Baldwin spoke in Edinburgh, strongly defending the government's and Locarno Treaty, saying that if treaty obligations are not fulfilled, Britain cannot guarantee peace, and cannot continue to reduce armaments. Those who like trouble and those who like to talk about war are merely instigating unrest. Land Minister Halesham spoke in Brighton, saying that Britain intends to reduce its armaments to the extreme. Today's British army is almost only a police force to protect the British Empire. It is important to know that in today's Britain, military strength is the most important guarantee of world peace. Aviation Minister London Terry spoke in Bristol, opposing Britain's continued reduction of armaments, believing that this would only make people more uneasy. At the same time, Lord Jacob declared that the current strength of the British Navy is woefully inadequate. In any case, naval strength must be increased. According to the British Naval Minister's statement in the House of Commons a few days ago, in view of the fact that the United States and Japan both want to build ten 10,000-ton cruisers, each equipped with fifteen 6-inch guns, after extremely careful consideration, they have to restore the 1933 program, which includes adding two new 9,000-ton cruisers. According to British naval experts, even if Britain adds two cruisers, it still cannot eliminate the extremely poor position of British cruisers. (National Telegraph, 18th)

Bombings Occur on the Same Day in Austria, Spain, and Egypt: University Suspends Classes, Food Industry Strikes

(London) Today, bombings occurred in Barcelona in Spain, Cairo in the Egyptian capital, and Innsbruck in Austria. The food industry in Barcelona began a strike a few days ago, affecting 90,000 people. Today, two electrical appliances in an electrical factory were destroyed by bombs. French Side Promotes Direct Negotiations: Parisian Times Expresses Concerns About Germany's Attitude

(Paris) One of the most fiercely debated issues among French people for the past fifteen years, whether direct negotiations can be conducted between Germany and France, is now once again in the limelight in French public opinion. Since the German people's self-determination election and the foreign policy debates in the French Parliament, the number of supporters of direct negotiations has suddenly increased, and their power is also on the rise. The Morning Post, which has a large circulation, has now suddenly become a propaganda organ for promoting direct negotiations. The reason for the Morning Post's sudden change in attitude, according to its own transmission, is that since the signing of the Treaty of Paris, the negotiations between Germany and France have been completely ineffective and extremely disappointing. To this day, other than those who are inclined to commit suicide, no one wants this kind of situation to continue. The report further stated that conducting negotiations with Germany does not necessarily require the conclusion of a treaty, but it would be beneficial to hear Germany's conditions and consider them without intermediaries. Furthermore, the newspaper run by French perfume king Coty also supports direct negotiations between Germany and France. (National Telegraph, 17th)

(Paris) French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour and French Representative Massigli went to Geneva with British Foreign Minister Simon in the same car tonight. The Parisian Times published an editorial on this matter, warning readers that the intention of the British and French politicians in going to Geneva together this time is to restore the Disarmament Conference and make it successful as soon as possible. However, the future is extremely difficult and huge, because the Disarmament Conference must first draft a treaty, and Germany must be able to accept it. As for Germany's future attitude, the newspaper is quite concerned, and said that if there are any surprising developments in the future, we should not be surprised. The report also said that in any case, no more concessions should be made to Germany to induce it to return to Geneva. However, all countries should act as the rear guard of the League of Nations, because the League of Nations is currently in its most difficult period. (National Telegraph, 17th)

(Nanjing) The case of the Huai River Guiding Committee borrowing 8 million yuan from the Gengkuan funds was stalled due to Song Ziwen's resignation. Recently, after Finance Minister Kong took office, the committee sent a letter urging the matter, and the Ministry of Finance has agreed to be responsible for the guarantee. What needs to be further negotiated is only how many millions of yuan will be borrowed from the existing Gengkuan funds and the Gengkuan funds that have not yet matured, and the distribution of principal and interest repayment methods. Once these procedures are negotiated, appropriation can begin. Regarding the engineering plan for guiding the Huai River upstream and downstream, the engineering department, based on the survey report, stated that the Shaobo Lake lock and the Huaiyin dike project are part of the entire engineering plan. Currently, the design team of the engineering department is planning to start collecting land and accurately calculate the engineering materials, how to purchase them, an estimate of the cost of materials, and preparations for hiring workers and management. Once the Gengkuan funds are appropriated, construction will begin. (Special Dispatch, 18th)

Negotiations on Pacific Company Directly Collecting Telegraph Fees

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications investigated that the Pacific Telegraph Company has been directly collecting telegraph fees from recipients for telegrams sent to the interior of our country and abroad. It was recently discovered that there are two places, Qingdao and Hankou. The telegrams sent to Hankou are marked with the letters BIP, but the telegrams sent to Qingdao are not marked. This telegram is directly charged, and the company calculates it at the US dollar price, charging a lower fee, privately negotiating, hoping to deceive the Bureau, absorb telegraphic services, and violate the contract, so it has contacted the company to negotiate, and has sent a circular to the bureaus, informing all merchants that all telegraph fees should be collected by the bureaus, and ordering the International Telegraph Bureau to report the details so that further negotiations can be carried out. (Special Dispatch, 18th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications revised the insurance measures for various telecommunications agencies, stipulating that insurance matters for various telecommunications agencies should be collected by the Ministry, publicly bid, and the cheapest one should be selected for insurance, and in accordance with the accounting year from July 1 to August 30 of the following year, one year should be taken as one period. In the future, more than 13,000 yuan can be saved each year. (Central News Agency dispatch, 18th)

The Huai River Conservancy Takes Over the灘蕩 (Tan Dang) and Lake Fields of the Huai River Basin

(Nanjing) In the past, the公地 (Public lands) of the 灘蕩 (Tan Dang) and lake fields in the Huai River basin were allocated by bureaus established by various provinces. The Huai River Conservancy, according to Article 4 of its organizational law, which stipulates that matters such as surveying, registration, requisition, and consolidation during the Huai River construction period shall be temporarily handled by the Conservancy, and having jointly formulated a 14-article outline of measures for consolidating the land in the Huai River basin with the Executive Yuan, has consulted with the governments of Jiangsu, Anhui, Shandong, and Henan provinces separately after being approved and put on record by the National Government, to negotiate the handover. Recently, considering that the construction sites for the two-year engineering plan are mostly located within Jiangsu Province, the Conservancy has first taken over the public lands of the Huai River basin in Jiangsu Province, with the consent of the Jiangsu Province. The Department of Finance has been instructed to transfer the files of the 灘蕩 (Tan Dang) and lake fields of the Huai River basin to the Conservancy for receipt. In addition to sending personnel to the Department of Finance to count, pack, and transport the files to Nanjing, the Conservancy also plans to send personnel to the original managing counties to implement the takeover. (Central News Agency, 18th)

Additional Telegraph Offices Established in Hebei

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications has instructed the Hebei Telecommunications Administration Bureau to establish additional telegraph offices in Luan County and Haiyang, eastern Hebei, to facilitate communication. It is reported that the branch offices have been formally established. In addition, a telegraph and telephone business office has also been added in Dongzhanzhen, Gong County, Henan. Shanxi Province Formulates Regulations for People's Obligatory Service

(Taiyuan) In order to vigorously promote various construction projects, the authorities of this province have recently formulated nine articles of regulations for the people's obligatory service, which were promulgated on the 17th and ordered to be implemented by all counties. The regulations are as follows: (1) In order to enhance the social prosperity and development of public undertakings in this province, the people of Shanxi have the obligation to perform public service. (2) People serving are limited to males aged 18 to 49. (3) The term of service for the people is limited to 13 days per year. The distribution of the types of work and dates is as follows: 1. Repairing roads: 10 days; 2. Planting trees and afforestation: 2 days. (4) The following personnel are exempt from labor service: 1. Current teachers and staff of schools at all levels; 2. Students currently studying at schools; 3. Active-duty soldiers; 4. Current civil servants and police officers. (5) People with illnesses should be exempted from service, but only if they have a certificate from the head of the管閭隣 (Guan Lu Lin neighborhood) and have obtained permission from the village head. (6) People serving in their villages and towns should provide their own meals. If serving more than 20 li (Chinese mile) outside the village, a meal allowance of less than one jiao (Chinese currency unit) will be issued. (7) People who are required to serve should be registered by the village or town administration based on the household survey table in January each year and sent to the county for work distribution. (8) When the county government distributes work to the people, it may, when necessary, order the heads of each district, village, and town to formulate the work items, locations, and labor requirements within their respective districts, villages, and towns and submit them for distribution. (9) These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 18th)

Five More Silk Factories Close in Shunde

Japanese Reporter Stationed in Russia Discusses the Perilous State of Japanese-Russian Relations - Subtly Criticizing the Failure of Japanese Diplomacy

▲ The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun on the 13th carried a telegram from Special Correspondent Fuse in Vladivostok, stating: "When I (Fuse refers to himself) was traveling in Moscow, I participated in the 15th anniversary celebration of the October Revolution last autumn and the anniversary celebration this spring, twice visiting the Red Square parade. At that time, hundreds of military aircraft were flying in formation over Moscow. On the morning of November 7th, I left Moscow for Vladivostok, but I did not forget to observe the 16th anniversary of the October Revolution, witnessing the spectacle of more than a dozen heavy bombers and a dozen fighter planes soaring together over the Golden Horn Bay. Recalling last autumn, a Russian leader said to me (Japan's) Plenipotentiary Matsuoka Yosuke, 'The Red Army's heavy bombers can fly over the Sea of Japan overnight, destroy the Japanese naval port of Sasebo, and slowly fly back to their bases in the coastal province.' Although this was a threat from Russia to Representative Matsuoka, its current strength can be imagined. Originally, the Russian government's foreign policy adopted a peaceful approach, so it repeatedly proposed to various countries to conclude non-aggression treaties, because Russia's defense still had shortcomings. However, this was only an observation of two or three years ago; today's situation is very different. It is inevitable that our country's (referring to Japan) foreign policy towards Russia has been mistaken. Why? In the past, Russia repeatedly proposed to us to conclude a non-aggression treaty, but it has not been realized to this day. Although Russia verbally advocates peace, it spares no effort in actually strengthening its national defense strength. When I was in Moscow, I often clearly questioned the Russian authorities, saying, 'If Japan and the United States were to go to war, would Russia attack Japan from behind?' And they all answered in unison, 'Socialist countries do not want to join wars between capitalist countries.' They also said, 'If this kind of behavior were to occur, we would have no face to face Lenin in the afterlife, and even loyal communist party members would deny taking advantage of the Japanese-American war to adopt an aggressive policy, hoping to benefit like a fisherman; if we were to abandon peaceful diplomacy and turn to an aggressive policy, Russia would not only have no benefits to speak of, but would also expose the flaws of Bolshevism,' and so on. In the past, when I stayed in Moscow, I participated in gatherings of important figures from Japan and Russia, and I heard Russians bring up the issue of renaming Vladivostok. Because many Russian cities have been renamed since the revolution, they planned to rename Vladivostok Uladiv-Gaugazhi, which means changing from aggression to peace. From this, it can be seen that Russia is inherently peace-loving. Unexpectedly, three Japanese planes suddenly appeared in the sky over Slavyanka, and Russia was greatly disturbed. In Xiongji Chong, Japan, strange planes also appeared. At the same time, the sky over the border between Korea and Russia suddenly presented an uneasy atmosphere of rumors and fear. Therefore, the most worrying thing at present is the rapid deterioration of Japanese-Russian relations and the occurrence of conflict. Looking back, Japanese-Russian relations have deteriorated considerably within a year, but when I arrived in Moscow, it was the period of improved Japanese-Russian relations. At that time, it was the Kherlen River incident, and Russia showed great goodwill towards Japan. Therefore, the Russian authorities warmly welcomed Plenipotentiary Matsuoka's visit to Moscow. At that time, Russia very much hoped to conclude a non-aggression treaty with Japan, but the Japanese government had been studying the pending non-aggression treaty for one or two years, and there has been no progress to this day, which is due to the lack of preparation for diplomatic negotiations. At that time, Russia emphasized the clear demarcation of the Russian-Manchurian border and that the Japanese-Manchurian treaty should not conflict with the Beijing Treaty and the Fengtian Treaty. However, Plenipotentiary Matsuoka had no preparation for negotiation, thus missing a good opportunity. When Matsuoka met with Litvinov, Karakhan, Radek, etc., it was a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity for good Japanese-Russian relations. Later, Ambassador Ota Sakei and Counselor Kaneko took office, reorganized the diplomatic lineup, and negotiated with Russia. Negotiations on the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway began, and Russia also rejected the invitation to form an alliance. Other issues were also gradually being discussed. Unexpectedly, the opportunity was lost, negotiations on the Chinese Eastern Railway stopped, the Manchurian-Russian conflict became increasingly pressing, and Japanese-Russian relations rapidly deteriorated. At this point, Russia released secret documents, and the rumors of a Japanese-Russian war spread around the world. For example, a news agency in a certain European country even telegraphed its special correspondent in Moscow, 'After the Japanese-Russian war breaks out, you should go to the front line as a war correspondent.' The precariousness of Japanese-Russian relations is such that their fate hangs by a thread."

Luo Wengan Arrives in Nanchang - Reports to Chiang Kai-shek on the Situation in Xinjiang

Nanchang correspondence: Luo Wengan, Minister of Foreign Affairs and Minister of Justice, arrived in Wan at 4:00 PM on the 15th. He also discussed with Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, and other members of the Central Supervisory Committee after arriving in Nanjing to resolve the political direction of Xinjiang and the border regions.
