Autumn □ Special Issue Late Autumn □

Late Autumn

— Ms. Wang Mei

Just past the Double Ninth Festival, it is late autumn again.

The leaves of the梧桐 (wutong) tree are painted red, and the branches begin to tremble. The scenery is so desolate, and the emotions are so dim. Late autumn brings aging to people.

I wander alone in this forest. I want to find, to find my childhood that was lost not long ago. Here in spring, I see flowers, red and white, blooming on the ground and in my heart. Here in summer, there are green leaves, sparse and dense, shading the fields and my body. Around me is a warm wind, and above my head is a bright sun, but now, now only the stream still flows, flowing into the bottomless abyss.

No spring, no summer, and no childhood that I left behind!

What can I find? The wind is so bleak, the grass is so withered and yellow. My heart flies to the ground with the fallen leaves, rustling! I trample on the fallen leaves, and also trample on my heart!

The crows return to their nests with lonely voices. There is a touch of afterglow in the sky, which reminds me of two lines of poetry I saw not long ago: Across the colored desert sky.

One lone bird flight

Perhaps this is late autumn, how dreary and tasteless late autumn is!

In the Season of Falling梧桐 (wutong) Leaves

— Yunshan

The sun has lost its previous violent heat, only redeeming a touch of pale yellow light. The autumn wind, a gust of sharp wind, blows with a howling sound, and it feels cold when it blows on the body, as if the cold air in the wind penetrates straight into the heart from the pores of the skin.

On the street, there are no longer women's crisscrossing jade legs, and at the same time, the thighs of ordinary, clumsy, and dark coolies are gradually disappearing among the crowds' hesitant footsteps. Autumn sales, woolen sales flags dance wildly in the wind above people's heads, sugar-roasted chestnuts, stir-fried hot白菓 (ginkgo nuts), crystal文丹 (mandarin oranges), Tianjin雅耳黎 (pears)... are arranged everywhere in front of people. Those friends sitting in the car, 丨丨 hiding their bodies in suits and loose robes, and those wrapping their snake-like bodies in coats, are all silently welcoming the approaching winter, 丨丨 because they or she needs to change the taste!

However, on the other hand, the common people who are being oppressed by the power of "dumping" must add the burden of "cold" to their shoulders; therefore, they must make a good deal with the longevity bank, 丨丨 continuously pawning summer clothes and exchanging winter clothes. The most miserable, of course, is the little urchin on the road. He has no loose robes or suits and coats, only a few broken burlap bags sewn together and wrapped around his flesh and blood. The broken burlap bags cannot block much of the cold wind, so he has to tear off the advertising paper on the wall to serve as temporary winter clothes, quilts, and hats. Otherwise, what better way is there? To rob? To peel pigs? Too dangerous! It's against the law. To steal? Not possible either. To commit suicide? Not worth it! I have the courage, but...

The autumn wind, a gust of sharp wind, blows with a howling sound, and it feels cold when it blows on the body, as if the cold air in the wind penetrates straight into the heart from the pores of the skin.

The洋梧桐 (sycamore) trees on both sides of the road also shed a few yellow leaves with the sound of the wind. Ah! Winter is coming! At the same time, the two different classes lurking in this world will reappear before our eyes, gradually, gradually, unfolding, expanding, and deepening!

Winter Clothing

— Yu Youqing

The west wind is blowing harder and harder, and the earth is gradually getting colder. That's right, after the windy and rainy Double Ninth Festival, the weather is much colder than before.

Thin lined clothes, of course, can no longer resist the cold, so cotton clothes and flannel shirts have risen in response to the season. Of course, people with money have no worries. They just need to keep a few tailors busy, working day and night, to provide the ladies with a try of new clothes. The winter clothes of 1933, of course, have a new style.

Several摩豋密司 (tailors) are holding flannel work in their hands, working diligently wherever they are. They are also making winter clothes very quickly.

But when we think of the Yellow River breach and the communist areas, where eating often becomes a problem, how can they take care of that? Therefore, those places are getting colder and colder every day, and their hearts are also breaking more and more every day. The west wind is blowing harder, and there is no winter clothing. How pitiful!

The young mistresses of the city change their winter clothes once a year, as if last year's winter clothes can no longer be worn. They have to be sent to the wet nurses to wear. So many winter clothes are only worn for one winter.

I heard that in Shaanxi and Gansu, not to mention winter clothes, it is said that their trousers cannot be worn by everyone. Compared with the young mistresses of the city, it is really "the judgment of clouds and mud."

When the proletariat sees the west wind blowing, it makes them feel sad, because after the west wind rises, they have to find ways to make or redeem winter clothes from the longevity bank.

Autumn Maples

— Xie Jizuo

"Autumn maples are no ordinary color, half tears and half blood," what a sorrowful and heroic sentence this is!

Autumn deepens! The maple forests of Qixia Mountain and the red leaves of Linggu Temple, I have admired them in the past, always feeling they were just autumnal adornments. My heart never felt any great symbolism; year after year, I passed them by indifferently. Now, the maple leaves in both places are still extraordinarily red, but the pigment of the red seems to carry some tragic darkness. The blazing sun shines on the leaf surfaces, reflecting an even more terrifying color, as if each maple leaf could be compared to China today, as pitiful as its state under the scorching sun.

"Autumn maples are no ordinary color, half tears and half blood," the whole of China is no longer an ordinary sight, but truly "half tears and half blood!"

After the West Wind Rises

— Shi Chun

Gusts of west wind blew up clouds of dust from the street. On the street, pedestrians involuntarily hunched their shoulders. I came out from Avenue Road, and the street was covered with a layer of sycamore leaves. Some were yellow, some were red. Small leaves struck my head, and I burst out from the falling leaves and walked into the northwest wind.

Many very fashionable women wore fur-collared coats, strutting on the road as if they didn't see the sycamore leaves falling, as if they didn't know that the northwest wind had blown upon them. I was only wearing a very thin jacket. Exposed to the face of the wind, it had lost its effectiveness in resisting the cold, and I felt a shiver.

Before long, I reached Xinzha Road. I couldn't bear it anymore and prepared to take a tram back to put on more clothes. After walking a few more steps, I reached the tram stop, where I stood waiting for the tram. But the tram seemed to have slowed down in the cold wind and didn't come for a long time, so I stood there.

In the corner of the surrounding wall, there was a pawnshop. Below the iron handle shaped like a "ruyi" scepter hung the original plaque with the character "Pawn" (當). I couldn't help but shift my thoughts from taking the tram to the pawnshop. My thoughts were completely enveloped by the "Pawn" plaque, everything I had.

From here, I saw two people who seemed to be wearing only single layers of clothing running into the pawnshop. Inside the door, there was a screen with the character "Pawn" on it, obscuring all the internal secrets. I didn't know what was happening inside. From here, I could only see the small sign at the entrance fluttering in the wind.

Soon, a man wearing a tattered long gown came out from behind the screen, looked around, and held a package wrapped in blue cloth, as if he were a thief afraid of being seen. Looking from here, I met his eyes. Ah, wasn't that Mr. Wang from next door? I hadn't seen him since he moved. How had he gotten like this?

As I was wondering, Mr. Wang suddenly disappeared. Mr. Wang's son had set up a business in Zhabei, and all of his assets were in that business. But it was completely destroyed by artillery fire last time. His son returned empty-handed and unemployed. Six months ago, they moved because they were gradually becoming impoverished, and since then, I didn't know where they had gone.

The tram came. I forgot the cold I felt. I no longer wanted to go back to put on more clothes. A girl wearing a leather coat walked by, bringing a gust of west wind.

Random Notes from a Journey to Wuxi 丨丨丨丨

— Yang An

The waves are calm, the shore faces the mist. The great and small Jishan Mountains are idle all day long. Two or three fishing boats chase after the water. In the slanting sunlight, a pair of birds return together. Such a landscape is never tiresome to behold. In a place of wide leisure, let us lean on the railing. Do not ask about the vicissitudes of human affairs; entrust oneself to optimistic views of the vastness of Kanghai.

Idle Gaze at Taihu Lake

The lake is broad, embracing dragons as they hasten. The peaks are numerous, and the mountains are not lonely. The sound of the waves harmonizes with the intensity of the rain. The force of the water is driven by the wind. The region divides Wu and Yue. The mountain mists exist between presence and absence. How can West Lake compare? Its grandeur and beauty are altogether different. (Sheng Bai said that the wonder of Taihu lies in its grandeur and vastness, while West Lake is beautiful and delicate, seemingly incomparable.)

Drunken Red Leaves

— Xu Benxi

Treading on autumn light, I arrived in Suzhou again. Suzhou is a place where I traveled before. I am already too lazy to listen to the bell of Hanshan Temple. Even if Mr. Yu Dafu sees the charm of "A sail in the rain passing Loumen" as very elegant, and how memorable it is to ride a donkey in the drizzle, slowly going along Qili Shantang to pay respects to Zhen Niang, my purpose for this trip is to see the red leaves of Tianping Mountain, so my lingering on the shores of Gusu Terrace seemed ordinary.

Indeed, taking advantage of the autumn twilight, when thick frost covers the shoulders of the maple leaves, ascending Tianping Mountain to see the mountains covered with red trees, no one would bear to leave. This is because the red maples have the allure of a fair lady in red makeup. And the posture of the sunset reflecting the red leaves, swaying in the bleak autumn wind, symbolizes the spirit of a warrior. Who among the wise would not marvel at the vibrant crimson that adorns a life filled with the dryness of autumn! An ancient poem says, "Stopping the carriage, I sit loving the maple forest at dusk; the frosted leaves are redder than the flowers of the second month." If not for a passionate person, who could say such moving words? Those who have not actually seen a forest of red leaves, who would know the greatness and sincerity of poetic meaning!

When we reached "A Thread of Sky," it was already late afternoon. The afternoon sunlight did not seem as spirited as in the morning, but precisely because of the dimness of the sunlight, the colors reflected on the clusters of red leaves were even more vibrant. "Ten Thousand Tablets Facing the Sky" originally had only emptiness and loneliness. The chaotic, bizarre rocks in the autumn with white dew and frost felt even more decayed and desolate. But because of the red trees on the cliffs, it felt as if a decadent old man had revived the joy of spring, uttering infinite melancholy. And the surrounding red maples, like intoxicated beauties, revealed the rosy blush of youth, charming nature. This painting, containing two kinds of emotions and vitality, already represents the two most successful and saddest stages of life. Even someone not prone to sentimentality cannot help but be moved to think of the joys and sorrows of life.

Autumn mountains and forests are originally full of the ashes of death. The rustling west wind, along with the whistling falling leaves, seems to be urging people to grow old. But in Tianping Mountain, there are blood-like red leaves to adorn the season of vanishing, allowing people to recapture the light of struggle from a declining state of mind. How magnificent is this power of incitement and enlightenment! Do red leaves exist simply to be sung by poets? While appreciating the red leaves, we must at least grasp the hints that the red leaves give us and move forward.

When we returned to the foot of the mountain, we saw a foreign woman sitting on the grass, painting. She was wearing light blue casual clothes, reflecting her white neck and hands. One look told you that she was someone who loved beauty very much. She gazed at the mountains and forests while contemplating and drawing. Looking at her draft, she had already sketched the outline of the mountain and evenly distributed the red leaves in appropriate places. Seeing her appreciation of the red leaves, we could at least determine that she was also a lover of red leaves.

The few red leaves I brought back, tucked in a book, were somewhat withered. I mourned their short lifespan and pondered for a long time.

Travel Log

The Waning Autumn of Xuanwu Lake

— Weizhong

It's Sunday, time to wander outside as usual. The weather is gloomy, but it's not raining. Hiding indoors would be even more boring. Lao Zhu and Ge proposed visiting Xuanwu Lake. We took a two-wheeled horse-drawn carriage with them at Xinjekou. On this wide pebble road, it was deserted, with few visitors! Autumn must be deep. The clip-clop of the horses' hooves echoed in the vast space, advancing with a steady rhythm.

Outside the city was a long embankment. We got out of the carriage and walked along the lake side.

Isn't this exactly the place that people yearn for as so-called historical sites and scenic spots? Yes, it is. Emperor Yuan of the Jin Dynasty practiced his naval fleet here. During the Yuanjia era of the Song Dynasty, a black dragon was seen here. Since ancient times, many poets and scholars have lingered here. But what about now? Even if you want to find a little bit of the remaining charm, it's almost impossible!

Passing Asia, wiping out Ge Bay, you reach America. The achievements of revolutionary construction are so amazing! Xuanwu Lake is no longer called Xuanwu Lake! It is said that "construction" has divided this place into the five continents of Asia, America, Europe, Africa, and Australia, calling it "Five Continents Park." Now, Xuanwu Lake has become a name in history.

America is the most outstanding place here, with the most modern structures, European and American-style houses, monuments that stand like ivory towers, flat sidewalks, patterned gardens, flowers everywhere, grass everywhere. It's a pity that it's not the time when a riot of colors compete in beauty and fragrance!

Zhongshan Hall, Yiyun Tower, and other places have also changed their appearance. The weather is cold, and people no longer need such cool places. A few tea servers are left, surrounding a square table, playing the game of chess.

The wind scrapes the water surface into layers of fish scales. Reflected by the faint sunlight, a few broken stems and remaining branches by the lake silently fell on the water.

"Hey!" Lao Ge shouted strangely in the bamboo forest over there. We hurried over. It turned out that he had discovered a kind of "bamboo pole literature" and was reading it with relish. Almost every bamboo pole here was engraved with tiny characters, from love affairs like "Ah Feng," "Yue," "Sister, I love you" to commemorative articles like "So-and-so visited here in such-and-such year and month," and even national affairs like "Resist Japan and save the country" and "Swear to recover lost territory." Almost everything was captured by these few bamboo poles. However, those who wrote "Resist Japan and save the country" accounted for less than one-tenth. Is it because the country is already peaceful and there is no need to resist Japan? Or are the friends who engraved the bamboo from another country?

Walking past, you reach Africa. Africa is not like America, with no modern buildings, no entire flower gardens, no entire grasslands, and no wide and flat sidewalks. America has been draped in the outer shell of 20th-century capitalism, while this place still fully preserves the prototype of a 15th and 16th-century agricultural society.

Clumps of artemisia and smartweed scattered randomly by the water, mixed with a few reeds with white heads. On the shore, bald mulberry trees and sparse bamboo hid one or two thatched huts. Strolling on this path overgrown with weeds, a kind of simple, natural, great, and mysterious power assailed the heart.

Further on, a very long embankment leads directly to Europe. A piece of withered and yellow weeds trembled in the west wind. Several cowherds and woodcutters bent over, hunching their backs, and crawled on the Australia surrounded by water. Several piles of broken walls and ruined tiles quietly collapsed nearby.

All of this scene was too desolate. Our poet, Lao Zhu, picked up a fallen leaf and wrote, "A desolate autumn heart," and casually threw it into the water. Slowly and slightly, it lay on the water surface, flowing and flowing, until a fallen lotus stem stopped it.

Desolation gnawed at the poet's heart, and Lao Zhu could no longer linger here! He urged us to go back, and on the long embankment we came to, we found the original carriage, climbed on, and the clip-clop of hooves spread the desolate mood of deep autumn in the empty and vast autumn sky.

Autumn is deep丨

Tax on Foreign Wheat and Flour Expected, Flour and Wheat Rise Sharply | Flour Up More Than Four Cents...Wheat Up More Than One Dime |

Yesterday, the flour market was initially showing signs of leveling off as Northern traders found it too high after several days of sharp rises and were less eager to buy. However, yesterday's news reported that the decision to tax foreign wheat had been made. This measure is inevitable and will definitely be implemented within the next one or two months. Therefore, the formal order may be issued soon. Due to this news, the market turned sharply upward. Although the price of foreign wheat was reported to be down 3, 4, 5, or 6 cents, and demand was particularly weak, the flour market rose step by step. Distant months were especially popular in the afternoon. Although the price of foreign wheat was reported to be down, there were no confirmed orders. However, Fuxin Factory again traded government-owned American wheat at a ship price of 4.25 yuan, and did not cover its position after taking delivery. Therefore, the closing price was up 4.5 cents for the second month, 4.25 cents for the third month, 4.75 cents for the fourth month, 3.25 cents for January, 1.25 cents for the current month, and 1.75 cents for February.

Yesterday, the wheat market rose across the board after the market opened because of reports of import duties on foreign wheat. Calculated as a percentage, wheat was up 5 jiao and flour was up 37.5 cents. It was difficult to place orders for foreign wheat today, the cost increased, and domestic supplies were insufficient. Therefore, public sentiment was very positive. All months rose in unison, and distant months soared even more in the afternoon due to the tax issue. The closing price was up as much as 14 cents for April, 12 cents for March, and 11 cents for February. Recent months also followed suit, with the current month and January up 2 cents each, and December up 4 cents. Spot wheat continued to rise, with Middle Gate up another 5 cents. Free Talk

New Facial Masks

— Tang Tao

It is said that influenced by the trend, the dramas on the literary stage have been changing one after another. Although the roles remain the same, the facial masks are brand new.

Those who used to play the roles of rich men and gentlemen now have to put on a sad face, twisting their noses and crying about poverty; those who used to play shrewish women and promiscuous women in triangle plays now also wear a serious face and play the role of the main male character in a cross-dressing performance. White-faced actors go back to the backstage to apply even whiter powder, and soon come on stage again; green-faced and fanged actors put on an unnatural smile, winking at the audience. All these, all these, are new, brand new.

Although old dramas still exist, they are newly decorated. Xue Pinggui recruits a son-in-law in the Western Liang, and Luo Hongxun sets up a ring in Yangzhou. In the past, they were martial arts dramas, but now they are performed by effeminate young male actors. But they can still use knives, spears, release hidden arrows, and challenge in a strange and exaggerated manner, cooing and whimpering.

So the audience cheered.

The facial masks are becoming more and more bizarre. Red, white, black, gilded: competing with each other, pulling and fighting fiercely, losing, going to repaint one and coming again. The last ones are foreign facial masks, with high noses and blue eyes, walking with straight legs, humming foreign Four Books and foreign Book of Rites in their mouths. If you don't believe it, please eat foreign fiery eyes. If you still don't believe it, airplanes, tanks, and rifles.

So the audience cheered again.

But facial masks also have other wonderful uses. The last time Xiao came to Shanghai, the literary people of Shanghai gave him a set of newly invented small facial mask models, and they were also stored in a box. Xiao happily took them away. It can be seen that facial masks can also be given to celebrities as gifts, asking celebrities to take them abroad to sow seeds, in order to be immortalized.

This is naturally limited to domestic products, and must be "newly invented."

Nobel Prize for Literature and the Vanquished

— Mu Mutian

Yesterday, I was talking about the Nobel Prize for Literature with an editor of a magazine, and then made a little joke, saying:

丨丨Will your esteemed magazine publish a "Manchurian Literature Special Issue"?

丨丨Then, you will be the greatest writer. Secondly, there is also Li Huiying, he said with a smile.

丨丨There is also Yang Hui. We are considered the "three great literary figures" of "Manchuria." I smiled as I said this.

This is a joke. But it aroused my infinite sadness and many questions.

It is said that this year's Nobel Prize winner, Pu Ning, is an "exile" who now lives in Paris. I feel that my situation has something in common with his. Although, I dare not nail the honorary title of "exile" to my head, but since the "September 18th Incident," I have been a "vanquished person." Moreover, Pu Ning lives in Paris in the West, and I live in Paris in the East. This time, Pu Ning won the prize, and I feel like I have also gained a little bit of glory. The Nobel Prize Committee can at least look up to the "vanquished."

The old Indian Tagore won a prize once. He is also a "vanquished person," because he lives in India, so we did not realize that he had the sadness of "vanquishing." So we also did not see how highly the Nobel Prize Committee valued him. However, this time, giving the prize to Pu Ning is indeed a "different look" from the committee members.

I think that in the future, if the committee members continue to follow this principle of "caring for" the "vanquished," then the "vanquished" will also have a way out. Not only will they be knighted, but they can also make a fortune. Gaining both fame and fortune, wouldn't that be the best of both worlds? If American black writers and African black writers have won awards, and in the end, it is "Manchuria's" turn, no matter which of our "three great literary figures" is knighted, I can always make a lot of money. Although I won't be promoted, I can still get rich. At that time, at least, I can eat a little more beef. Because we are all good friends, whether Yang Hui is knighted or Li Huiying receives the prize, I can always get a little bit of the gravy.

However, Pu Ning doesn't seem to be a very remarkable writer. Kuprin, a well-known Kuprin, doesn't seem to have been knighted. If you ask if there are any great writers in the world who have not been knighted, isn't there André Gide in France? There is still Gorky in Russia. However, not giving it to Gide or Gorky, but giving it to Pu Ning, proves that the Prize Committee is not judging people by their works, but by their status. Then, aren't the "three great literary figures" of "Manchuria" even more hopeful?

What is strange is that since Tagore was knighted, other writers who have lost their country but have not become "exiles" have not won the prize. Last year, the Nobel Prize was given to the American Lewis, and none of the black slave writers, such as Hughes, received the prize. What is going on? If it is not based on the value of the works, then the treatment of "vanquished" people is unequal.

But why is the treatment of "vanquished" people different? "Vanquishing" is "vanquishing" everywhere. It is probably because the ways of "vanquishing" are different, and the natures of "vanquishing" are different. In that case, the "three great literary figures of Manchuria" can also give up hope.

It is feared that "vanquished people" like us cannot be sympathized with by the Nobel Prize Committee.

Lodging House

— Xu Zhuanpeng

The sun was about to set. Wang Er, melancholically lost in thought, sat on the doorstep, striking a flint to light his pipe.

A dilapidated, dark, and damp small house had just been whitewashed with lime. The four crooked black characters "Accommodation for Merchants" were written on the whitewashed wall above the door. Inside, the wooden walls and pillars were also whitewashed, trying to conceal the dilapidated and filthy flaws of the small house. Wang Er had repaired this broken house to revitalize his business. He borrowed some money, added some secondhand cotton wadding and secondhand bedsheets from a used clothing store, and hired a carpenter to repair the rickety or almost dismantled bed frames. Because he wanted to increase the lodging fee from twelve copper coins a night to twenty copper coins. However, since then, fewer and fewer lodgers had stepped over his threshold. Even the few regular customers had switched to other lodging houses.

Whenever the sun set, he sat melancholically lost in thought on the doorstep. In front of him was an official road leading to a city fifty miles away. Some people had bought goods from the city, carrying wicker baskets and sacks full of cloth... Some, with shoulder poles bearing heavy loads, had their backs bent, panting like oxen; some walked with a limp. Everyone needed to rest, but they all did not stop their forward steps.

"It's getting late, stay here!"

Wang Er sat on the doorstep, flashing a smiling face to everyone who passed by.

"It's not completely dark yet, we can still see the road!"

In this way, those who knew him, returned him a bitter smile and passed on.

If Wang Er saw people carrying heavy burdens, with frustrated expressions on their faces, he would change his tone and say to them with great sympathy:

"Ah, friend, you're carrying such a heavy load... so heavy... probably two hundred catties... don't push yourself too hard, rest, sit down..." As soon as someone took a breath, they rested. The first thing they said was:

"The city is conscripting soldiers again... two thousand of them... tens of thousands of soldiers..."

As soon as the speaker said this with a serious face, many people would come to listen.

"I heard that people wearing long gowns aren't being conscripted. People who wear long gowns have it easy in this world... Villagers who heard the news are afraid to enter the city and are fleeing back halfway. There's no business in the city either. If villagers don't enter the city, what will the city people eat? City people are also having bad luck these days..."

As the conversation lengthened, they asked each other and talked about: rebellion, war, soldiers and bandits clashing, famine, cannibalism...

The passersby stood up, looked at the sky, the evening colors were hazy, night was approaching,

"Goodbye, boss!"

"Stay here! I have new cotton wadding and new straw mats... It's getting dark, stay here..."

However, Wang Er could not keep the customers. "New cotton wadding" and "new straw mats" could not entice them anymore.

In the evening, the lodging house that had once been revitalized had not a single lodger.

Wang Er said to his wife:

"These days, very few small businesses come and go; cattle dealers, tea merchants, fortune-telling blind men are also fewer; those who sell fake medicine, those who want to perform magic tricks, those who exchange chicken feather candy, they all stay in temples and ancestral halls, not in lodging houses..."

"Then why did you borrow money to repair the house and add cotton wadding..."

His wife spoke with a questioning tone. Wang Er had nothing to answer, only turned his head and sighed deeply.

On "Flower Drum Opera"

— Ye Dejun

Mr. He Ru’s three articles on "The Origin of Flower Drum Opera" cite numerous books and claim that Flower Drum Opera originated from the "Yagu Opera" and "Daya Hu" of the Song Dynasty, because the sounds of the three are similar and the events are similar, so they are three names for the same thing.

In addition to Meng Yuanlao's "Tokyo Dream Records" and Yunlu Manchao's records of the customs of Daya Hu, Wu Zimu's "Dream Liang Records" also has the same record, ending by saying: "It also means to drive away evil spirits." This is clearly a ritual of the great exorcism at the end of the year to drive away plague ghosts. Later, beggars played the story of Zhong Kui exorcising ghosts at this time to collect money. Huang Shi's "A Study of the Great Exorcism at the End of the Year" cites the Fuzhou Gazetteer, saying: "At the end of the year, the villagers perform exorcism. It has existed since ancient times. Now, the people of the state regard it as Daya Hu..." The customs of Fuzhou are precisely a continuation of the Song Dynasty's legacy. We can certainly consider Daya Hu as a kind of entertainment, but it is an old custom of the great exorcism, while playing the flower drum is, on the one hand, a livelihood for the Fengyang people who wander the streets and perform arts, and on the other hand, the audience regards it as purely entertainment. Regardless of whether Daya Hu has lyrics or not, its lyrics and the lyrics of the flower drum are definitely different. Even if there are, they are only about exorcising ghosts, while the flower drum songs are, as Tong Fumin said, "mostly lewd words." The roles in the flower drum opera... From these points of view, Daya Hu and playing the flower drum are not the same thing. The similarity between the two is that they are both means of livelihood for the poor. Since the events are not similar, the similarity of the sounds is even more unreliable. Regarding the saying that it originated from Yagu, the author has already said that "it is not easy to determine." If it is said that Yagu began with Prince Zichun, it does not match the wild art of Flower Drum Opera, and the two are also not the same thing. In short, the theory that Flower Drum Opera predates Zaju and Chuanqi is doubtful. I feel that its origin is close to the period of Peking Opera. If it had existed earlier, it would have become orthodox like Peking Opera, but although its power in folk dissemination is very large, it is still immature, which is precisely the form of wild art that has not transformed into orthodoxy.

I think its origin is that there were lyrics for playing the flower drum first, such as "The painted flower drum has round heads..." which is sung while playing the flower drum; then there was Flower Drum Opera, and what it performed was about playing the flower drum, such as the Peking Opera's "Playing the Flower Drum" and Hunan's "Wang San Sells Milk." In my hometown, whenever there is a welcoming god festival, there must be one or two Flower Drum troupes before the main event. Each troupe has seven or eight to a dozen people, and what they perform is nothing more than ordinary stories, but there is no playing of the flower drum. Each person does not tie five or six feet long wooden sticks to their feet, and they only walk back and forth when performing, which is a silent drama without lyrics. As for those who use seven or eight feet long wooden sticks, they are not called Flower Drum troupes, but are called "Stilt Walking." Judging from its name, it has some connection with playing the flower drum. This is another transformation of it.

He Ru's comment: Daya Hu also means to drive away evil spirits. Wu Zimu's words are correct, but he did not say that this is what is called exorcism in ancient times, because it is still different from exorcism. But if you consider exorcism as Daya Hu's predecessor, it is certainly acceptable, just as I consider Daya Hu as Flower Drum's predecessor. In fact, what I said about the relationship between Flower Drum Opera and Daya Hu Yagu is still from the closest point of view. If we trace it back to its distant source, it would not be limited to discussing shamanic dances and the great exorcism. However, the establishment of an art takes the essence and uses it broadly, intricately and complexly. If you insist on seeking it in one way, a historian with common sense would probably not do so. What I mean by originating from something is a more modest and hypothetical way of speaking, as a theory for imagination. What does Mr. Ye think of my humble opinion?

Two Brothers (33)

— Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

It is true that Mrs. Lu Zuimi's intelligence was limited, but she had the touch, smell, and subtle senses of women. However, she had never suspected this. She had generously raised her glass to bless Maraisha's soul in heaven. If she had had any suspicion, she would never have done that. Now he no longer doubted. The unconscious dissatisfaction with the wealth that had fallen on his younger brother and the love for his mother undoubtedly inspired his prudence, a commendable, filial, and yet somewhat exaggerated prudence.

When he came to this conclusion, he felt satisfied as if he had done a good deed. He decided to be kind to everyone, first to his father, because his father's muddled judgments, vulgar opinions, and overly conspicuous ordinariness often made him angry.

He was not late for lunch, and with his wit and cheerful mood, he made the whole family happy. His mother was very happy and said to him:

"My Pierre, you don't know how mischievous and interesting you are when you're happy."

He spoke eloquently, using strange words to describe their friends vividly, making everyone laugh. Bo Qiru was made the target of his ridicule, and Mrs. Lu Zuimi was also teased a few times, but he spoke with measure, joking without being cruel. He looked at his younger brother and thought to himself, "You fool, come and defend her; it's useless for you to be rich, I will suppress you when I'm happy."

While drinking coffee, he said to his father:

"Are you using the 'Pearl' today?"

"No, my child."

"Can I go have fun with Ginba on it?"

"Of course, you can go as much as you want."

He bought a good cigar at the first tobacco shop he came to and then walked happily to the pier.

He looked at the bright, shining, light blue sky, which seemed cool after being swept by the sea breeze.

The sailor Papagri, nicknamed Ginba, was dozing in the boat. When Roland didn't go fishing in the morning, Papagri had to prepare the boat for sailing at noon every day.

"We two are going, captain!" Pierre called.

He ran down the iron ladder on the river bank and jumped onto the small boat.

"What wind?" he said.

"The gentle southerly wind, Mr. Pierre. The wind on the sea is very good today."

"Then, old man, let's go."

Amateur Discussions

Ideal and Fantasy

— Gongpu

Recently, I often talked with the students of the supplementary school of this newspaper office, and heard many interesting discussions. The scope of these opinions is very broad, ranging from the country's internal affairs and diplomacy to personal life and ideals, all of which are fully expressed. However, comparatively speaking, most people pay more attention to personal issues, and very few opinions are put forward on general political and social issues. The reason for this is not that the current national crisis and social chaos are not enough to attract their attention, but that some people feel that their words are insignificant and that thinking too much will only increase their troubles and will not be of any practical benefit. Some people feel that people in the government have no way to solve the problem, so we people with little knowledge and experience naturally have no way to solve it. Still others have never thought about these issues at all, because they lost their education in the countryside in their childhood and came to Shanghai to live the life of an apprentice. In addition to working hard all day long, they have to be busy with self-study work if they have any spare time, so how can they have time to pay attention to national affairs? Some people say that the Chinese people's national concept is very weak, but judging from the above facts, the so-called lack of attention to national affairs by the people is not due to any innate nature, but is actually caused by the living environment. Therefore, what the reporter encourages and exhorts to these students is that under these different living environments, we all have different degrees of national concepts, which are difficult to unify. However, at least we should have an ideal in our personal lives as a goal for our work, career, and struggle. Otherwise, our lives will inevitably fall into a boring and meaningless state.

When it comes to ideals, they are absolutely different from fantasies. An ideal is a planned attempt based on the existing environment and one's own interests and abilities, while a fantasy is a lucky illusion that is not based on facts and has little possibility of being realized. For example, if a person has an ideal of becoming a chemist, then this person must usually be interested in chemistry, and must have a planned effort in the research of chemical theories and the exploration of experiments. Only in this way can it be called an ideal. If a person has no interest in chemistry, nor a plan for step-by-step research, nor the spirit of tireless experimentation, and wants to become a chemist, then it is a fantasy, a delusion, and is as absurd as the current group of people who hope to win a huge prize of 500,000 with ten yuan.

We know that fantasies are illusory and lucky, and carry a little mystery, while ideals rely on long-term practical efforts and struggles, and cannot be achieved overnight. Ideals have the demand for striving forward, while fantasies are mostly absurd thoughts after frustration and disappointment. We deeply feel that there are far more people with fantasies than people with ideals in today's society, which is enough to indicate that the entire society has entered a state of frustration and disappointment. So how should we save the decline of this society? This is of course not a question that can be answered in a few words, but in summary, it can be said like this: We should not fantasize, but establish an ideal. We should not be disappointed by the darkness of this society. We should deeply realize that there is light when there is an ideal, and there is life when there is an ideal. Our ideal is the vitality of society.

Life

Returning to the Countryside

— Ding Boping

(Farmer) I used to work in a factory in Shanghai. Because I had several illnesses and because of my mother's death, I owed three hundred yuan in debt. The interest on each yuan was four hundred wen per month. Before, I could use my wages as interest. Later, because the factory's production was surplus and its business was stagnant, my wages and working hours were reduced. Therefore, I could not pay the interest, and my life became dangerous. Even if I asked the capitalists to restore my wages, the factory also paid close attention to me, so I could not stand firm.

Last year, during the Mid-Autumn Festival in August, creditors came to my door almost every day, forcing me to run around like a stray dog, without any way out. In desperation, I fled to my cousin's house in the countryside in the late spring and early summer of this year. I entered that short and dark grass house with poor ventilation and ate a bowl of tea brewed in a pottery pot, which had a smoky smell. This was exactly the busy season for farming. The farmers were planting rice seedlings in the deep paddy fields, working so hard that they were covered in mud and sweat, without a moment's rest. Women also had to draw water under the scorching sun. When the sun set in the west, my cousin's parents returned from the fields for dinner. I remember eating egg soup, tofu dregs, celery, and stinky pickled cabbage, which was considered the number one dish to treat guests in the countryside. Her father had to get up early tomorrow, so he went to sleep after eating. As a rule, they would go to sleep as soon as it got dark. Almost all the villagers ate three meals a day, two meals of rice and one meal of porridge. Some also ate one meal of wheat rice, one meal of rice, and one meal of porridge. Breakfast time was around 7 o'clock, lunch time was marked by the sun being in the middle of the sky, and dinner was eaten when it was dark. After eating, there was nothing else to do besides sleeping.

From that day on, her family had to make some countryside snacks for me every day, and add some eggs and tofu for me when I ate. Such preferential treatment really made me feel uneasy, and the idea of "those who eat must work, and those who do not work should not eat" inevitably arose in my mind. So I decided to go to the fields the next day to help them work. It happened that the rice paddies were weeding these days. I borrowed a grass knife and a very large wide-brimmed straw hat from the neighbor. The next day, I woke up when the sky was about to dawn, changed my clothes, rolled up my trouser legs, took off my shoes and socks, and took the grass knife and straw hat and set off with her father. When we arrived at the rice paddy, they went down into the field, and I also went down into the field in their manner. The coolness of the mud and water penetrated my heart. I lowered my head and bent my back, and it took me a long time to take a step. Before weeding, each rice paddy had been fertilized to help the rice seedlings grow. The field I was weeding was very large, and the fertilizer was applied very heavily, which smelled terrible. When I used more force in the water, the fertilizer water often invaded my mouth or face. In addition, the friction of the rice seedlings made my arms red. The heat of the sky, the steam of the water, and the stench of the fertilizer were really unbearable. It was almost as hard as this for more than ten days. At first, it was just a moment of excitement, but later it was hard to refuse to do it. The skin on my arms and back peeled off, and I was as black as a Red Head A San (derogatory term for Indians). I also lost weight, and it was more strenuous than in the factory. The temperature was over one hundred and twenty degrees Fahrenheit, and the rice paddies were short of water. The farmers everywhere were busy drawing water day and night. Sometimes I also helped to move the waterwheels, and it took a lot of effort to turn these waterwheels. After drawing water for a few days, the sky still didn't rain. None of the villagers didn't say, "Good Bodhisattva, God gives us food, please give us some rain! Otherwise, there will be no harvest this year." They were extremely superstitious, so the elders in the village discussed asking for rain, and carried out the "Dragon God Bodhisattva" in the village temple for a parade. The nearby villagers all carried the old and the young, carrying hoes, burning incense, beating gongs, and lighting firecrackers to pray that the "Dragon God Bodhisattva" would bestow rain. At that time, infinite sorrow was aroused in my heart. Ah! Drought is a warning that the village panic is about to come! I, who was driven from the city's recession to the countryside, where will I find a place to return in the future?

Famous Articles and Speeches

Pan Yangyao on Revolutionary Occupations

— Recorded by Zhu Yuxiang

Technical nature As the saying goes, "Accumulating wealth of thousands is not as good as having a skill." For example, the poor people in the Jiangbei area make various small toys for children out of paper pulp, bamboo strips, and wood scraps, and sell them on the streets, which can also be used to make a living. Another example is in Hangzhou, there is a person nicknamed "Little Monkey". He is famous throughout the city for making small monkeys specifically for children to play with. He makes a decent living, and has accumulated some savings over the years, enough to keep him warm and fed. From this, it can be seen that the close relationship between technology and occupation cannot be separated. The year before last, after Mr. Zhang Gongquan returned from inspecting industries in Japan, he wanted to visit factories in our country. It happened that I also had this intention, so we went together. We specifically visited many yarn factories and asked why the Chinese yarn industry has been declining to such an extent recently. The person in charge of the factory replied that this is partly a technical problem. It is said that a yarn factory in Japan with 10,000 spindles only needs to hire 250 workers. But in China, even Shenxin needs to hire 350 workers to do the job. Other smaller factories often need to hire 400 to 500 workers, and a yarn factory in Zhengzhou, Henan, even needs to hire as many as 600 workers. The same production volume, but the number of workers employed differs so much. The number of workers increases, and the wages increase accordingly, so the cost is also high. How can we compete with Japanese goods? No wonder we are doomed to failure! In Japanese yarn factories, each worker can manage up to 37 spinning machines, while Chinese workers can only manage about 20 machines at most. Currently, the market price of Japanese yarn is 24 yuan per piece, while Chinese yarn, even Shenxin's, has to sell for 36 yuan per piece, and it is already very difficult. Other factories have to sell for 40 yuan per piece to maintain costs. Everyone, think about it, if we don't start from the root and actively make occupations technical, so as to compete with foreigners, no matter how much we boycott Japanese goods, it will be of no avail. Who doesn't want to buy cheap goods? Who cares whether it is Japanese or domestic?

Creativity Chinese people like to eat ready-made meals and are always unwilling to put in any effort to create. In the 16th year of the Republic of China, my brothers, Mr. Jiang Wenyu, Mr. Yang Weiyu, and Dr. Liu Zhanen, the current president of Shanghai University, and others initiated the establishment of a vocational guidance center. It has been six years now and has achieved some results. Every day, there are always more than 20 or 30 young people who come to the center to ask for job introductions. According to statistics, about 7,000 or 8,000 people have been successfully introduced by our center, which can be regarded as a small contribution to society. Among the young people we come into contact with every day, the level of education varies. Some have just graduated from elementary school and want to find a job. Some are high school graduates, and some are college graduates, and even some have returned from studying abroad. Often, many young people ask me to introduce them to work in banks, as if this is the only occupation in their ideal. However, I always advise them not to just eat ready-made meals, but to do what others have not done. One day, a young man who graduated from the mechanical engineering department of a university came to me to introduce him to a job. I casually picked up a pen holder on my desk and asked him if he could manufacture this, because almost all of the ones sold on the market are foreign goods. He thought it made sense, so he actively proceeded and raised 5,000 yuan of capital. Now he has opened a small factory to manufacture, and there may be hope in the future. Last year, my brothers and I founded a "China Credit Investigation Office" because we felt that there was a real need for it in society. At that time, the scale was very small, with only five or six staff members. The speed of progress in the past year has been beyond expectations. Due to the sharp increase in affairs, the number of staff members has been increased to 40 or 50, and there are also more than 20 basic members. There are as many as 70 or 80 foreign merchant companies and others who entrust credit investigation. It can be seen that engaging in this kind of business is more meaningful and hopeful than sitting around and eating ready-made meals and sticking to old businesses!

Small Social Model

Young, Away from Home, Old Coming Back – (Women's Prison)

— Ms. Li Xiaoqin

In a year of calamity and a month of misfortune, I, a humble shop assistant, was arrested and imprisoned in January of the 17th year of the Republic of China due to a certain case, and only regained my freedom in November of the 22nd year of the Republic of China. Now, I will truthfully recount my personal experiences of prison life, dividing it into four categories: clothing, food, hygiene, and work, as follows. However, since I am a female prisoner, my description will be particularly detailed regarding the women's prison. However, I believe that the conditions in the men's prison can only be worse than in the women's prison, and not better, because: first, this has been the custom in China throughout history; second, the women's prison is relatively free from overcrowding; third, female prisoners do not wear instruments of punishment.

Speaking of clothing in prison life, the only thing prisoners can enjoy is tattered cotton-padded coats that are not washed all year round, stripped from the dead and worn by the living. The cotton inside is knotted and cannot be loosened. If you wear it, a large lump will grow in some places; in others, only a single layer of fabric remains. It cannot be taken apart and washed, because it is too rotten, and once taken apart it will disintegrate and no longer be considered clothing. But even with such dirty old clothes, there are only a few dozen pieces, and many cannot get them or wear them. As for the new clothes donated by philanthropists, prisoners cannot wear them. Some are replaced by the guards with old, written-off prison clothes, and the new ones are exchanged for money to buy opium. Some are kept by the prison officials, and only when visitors come are they given to the prisoners to wear to make a grand appearance and demonstrate the achievements of the administration. If there are visitors and there are not enough new prison clothes for the prisoners to wear, then the prisoners without new clothes are driven to the latrine to avoid being seen.

As for food, because prisoners' meals are rationed by weight (22 ounces for criminal prisoners, 24 ounces for political prisoners), our clever prison officials mix rotten yellow rice with white pebbles and give it to the prisoners to eat. Once, when I was sick, I was granted special permission to eat slowly (because ordinary prisoners have a fixed time to eat, limited to only a few minutes), so I picked out the pebbles. The result was that the ratio of pebbles to rice was one to one. If someone suspects and says, "How can so many pebbles be excreted?" Then I cannot explain the reason, but my description above is absolutely true. Perhaps these pebbles have been researched by prison experts and can be mixed as food! Or perhaps it is the same as the Guanyin clay eaten by people in famine-stricken provinces such as Shaanxi and Gansu? However, the prisoners all feel that they have considerable constipation, which may be related to this. The rice is like this, and the vegetables are even worse. Each person gets such a small piece of rotten yellow vegetables for each meal, just for decoration. As for the filth in it, it is even more unbearable to ask about. When it rains, earthworms can be eaten out of the vegetables, and newspaper scraps are commonplace. Each person gets three bamboo tubes of water to drink every day, and there is no tea. Only in the summer are there two weeks of boiled barley water to drink.

Speaking of hygiene in prison, how can Chinese people have such good fortune! In the summer, each time over one hundred and sixty people share only three buckets of water for bathing. How can you wash with this? There are two visits from the doctor every week, but it is very dangerous to talk about taking medicine. If you have heatstroke, you don't get heatstroke medicine, but you are given alum water to drink. For headaches and fever, a whole pot of unknown Chinese medicine is boiled and each person is given a bowl to drink, without asking about the differences in the diseases. When you are seriously ill and enter the ward, it is really calling you to wait for death. There is no medicine there, and no one to take care of you, so prisoners are very afraid of entering the ward when they are seriously ill. If the guards hear a sick prisoner groaning loudly, disturbing their peace, they only need to threaten the sick prisoner, saying, "If you continue like this, I will send you to the ward!" If the prisoner has not lost consciousness, he will not dare to groan again. From this, you can see the awe of the ward.

The work can be divided into two parts, namely: (1) piecework. If you make a woolen sweater for someone, you can earn two or three yuan in wages outside, but the prison only gives us fifteen copper coins. Making socks, sewing the sock heads, each dozen gets fifteen cash, which is one and a half copper coins. (2) long-term work, that is, working in a factory specially set up in the prison, working twelve or thirteen hours a day. It is said that each prisoner can get a dime or so of wages every day, but this wage is nominally saved, but in reality, prisoners can only buy things once a month, opening an account for five hundred wen. The rest cannot be used at all, and the prisoners are not given an account on holidays to know how much they have saved. Then, where did the wages go? Most of those who do long-term work are sentenced to life imprisonment or more than ten years of imprisonment. Some of them die of illness in a few years, and some have no hope of ever being released. Even if they can be released, this muddled account cannot be cleared, and who dares to clear it? Only God knows this.

There is one more thing, that is, we women inevitably have our periods once a month, but each time when our period comes, the guards only give us twenty pieces of paper (four inches square). How can this be used in a week? So we have to use rotten dirty cloth instead. Some get poisoned and sick because of this, and some are discovered by the guards and suffer cruel punishment, saying that they have torn up public clothes, an unforgivable crime.
